# ctarnidd

A small repository of original, long-form market research articles. Article filenames are
date-stamped (`YYYY-MM-DDThhmm-<slug>.md`) to record when each was published.

## Articles

### [Take-Two's $44 billion market cap is one game, one date, and a $7.4 billion hole](2026-06-22T1100-take-two.md) · _2026-06-22_

Take-Two sells the most anticipated product in entertainment history and still loses money — a $298.2 million GAAP net loss for the fiscal year ended March 2026, sitting atop a $7.36 billion accumulated deficit that no run of "record net bookings" has erased. The entire ~$44 billion equity is a binary option on one date: Grand Theft Auto VI on November 19, 2026, already slipped three times across roughly eighteen months. The bookings-versus-GAAP wedge — driven by standard, legal deferred-revenue accounting, not fraud — lets management headline records while the bottom line stays red. At $239 a share against a ~$279 consensus target, you are accepting mid-teens upside for multi-hundred-percent downside on any delay or botched launch. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [National Grid books record £11.6bn capex and 78p EPS, but a £44bn debt load funds the dividend](2026-06-22T1030-national-grid.md) · _2026-06-22_

National Grid's FY2026 scorecard reads like a defensive investor's dream: underlying operating profit up 9% to £5.7bn, underlying EPS up 8% to 78.0p, a CPIH-linked dividend lifted to 48.49p, and a £70bn five-year build plan promising 8–10% annual EPS growth. The forensic reading is colder. The company spent a record £11.6bn — more than double its operating profit — financed by £2.8bn of fresh borrowing that pushed net debt to £44.2bn at 61% gearing. The "growth" is regulated capital growth someone must finance, with returns Ofgem (RIIO-T3's 6.12% real cost of equity), not the market, sets. Two years after a dilutive £7bn rights issue and ~15% dividend rebase, this is a leveraged bet on a regulator's generosity dressed as a bond proxy. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Okta's growth halves to 11% while the GAAP-to-adjusted gap swallows half its profit](2026-06-22T1000-okta.md) · _2026-06-22_

Okta, the identity vendor that once compounded revenue above fifty percent a year, grew just eleven percent in the quarter ended April 2026, with full-year FY2027 guidance pointing lower still at nine to ten percent — the slowest trajectory in its public history. The deceleration is dressed in 26% non-GAAP margins, record free cash flow, and a backlog past $4 billion, but the cleaner current-RPO read grew only twelve percent, offering no acceleration. Okta earned $74 million GAAP last quarter versus $168 million non-GAAP — a ~$94 million wedge that is mostly stock-based compensation. Meanwhile Microsoft bundles competing Entra ID free into M365/Azure, and a new-product carousel still reads as demonstration, not deployment. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [TD's Record Quarter Hides the Felony Asset Cap Strangling Its Only Growth Engine](2026-06-22T0930-toronto-dominion.md) · _2026-06-22_

Toronto-Dominion printed a quarter the bulls will quote for a year: adjusted earnings of $4.2 billion, adjusted EPS of $2.38 up 21%, revenue of $16.04 billion, record Canadian retail profit, a 4% dividend hike, and ~19 million shares retired. The colder machine beneath: TD is the first bank in U.S. history to plead guilty to conspiracy to commit money laundering — an adjudicated guilty plea carrying roughly US$3.09 billion in penalties and an unprecedented, indefinite OCC asset cap pinning its U.S. retail balance sheet near US$434 billion. These are settled facts. The bank is now selling up to $50 billion of securities, shrinking its U.S. footprint ~10%, and funding AML remediation through 2027. A bank growing EPS by buying back a frozen franchise is not growing. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Workday's Subscription Growth Has Slipped to 14% While the Machines It Sells Eat Its Own Seats](2026-06-22T0900-workday.md) · _2026-06-22_

Workday is the back-office operating system for much of the Fortune 500, and for a decade it grew subscriptions at twenty-plus percent. That metronome has slowed: subscription revenue grew 14.3% to $2.354 billion in the quarter ended April 2026, and full-year FY2027 guidance points to just 12–13%. The company sells seats — billed by the headcount that logs in — at the exact moment it is loudly selling AI agents built to do that back-office work without the headcount, and cutting its own staff to prove it. Beneath a 31.8% non-GAAP operating margin sits a 13.3% GAAP margin: non-GAAP EPS of $2.66 versus GAAP EPS of $0.87, with stock comp near 16% of revenue the main bridge. A maturing franchise asked to survive the thing it markets. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Lockheed Martin burned cash in Q1 2026 while paying out a compounder's multiple](2026-06-22T0830-lockheed-martin.md) · _2026-06-22_

Lockheed Martin reported Q1 2026 revenue of $18.0 billion — flat — and EPS of $6.44, down roughly 12%, but the line that matters sits lower: free cash flow swung to negative $291 million, a striking outcome for a stock the market prices as a serene dividend compounder. Strip away the record $194 billion backlog and the 191 F-35 deliveries and a harder story emerges — a contractor whose entire FY2025 sales growth traced to one airplane, whose margins are eaten by fixed-price programs it cannot reprice, and whose own executives now concede $500–700 million a year of classified-program cash burn through 2027. The "non-recurring" charges have become recurring guidance; the buyback keeps the per-share line tidy as the denominator shrinks. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Nucor's $3.23 quarter is built on a 50% tariff wall, not a wider moat](2026-06-21T1800-nucor.md) · _2026-06-21_

Nucor printed $743 million of net earnings and $3.23 a share in Q1 2026 — a 264% jump off a battered comp — on $9.50 billion of revenue, record seven-million-ton shipments, and operating margin snapping back to 12% from 4%. The headline reads best-in-class American steelmaker; the engine was a 14% jump in average selling price per ton and an import share crushed from 22% to roughly 15% by a 50% Section 232 tariff wall Washington can lower with a signature. Strip the policy and the comp, and Nucor remains a commodity price-taker breathing in and out with hot-rolled coil and the construction cycle. The bull case capitalizes a tariff-protected spike toward a $6.7 billion through-cycle EBITDA target as if the harvest never ends. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Ferrari shipped fewer cars again — and trades at 34x betting it never needs to ship more](2026-06-21T1730-ferrari.md) · _2026-06-21_

Ferrari delivered 3,436 cars in Q1 2026, down 4.4% from a year earlier, yet revenue still rose to roughly €1.85 billion because each car carried more options, personalization, and a richer country mix — a 39.1% EBITDA margin welded to an automaker. Net profit was flat at €413 million. That is the entire bull case: fewer units, fatter margins, an order book stretching into 2027. But at 34 times earnings, Ferrari is priced not as a cyclical maker of combustion supercars but as a perpetual-pricing-power machine that can cap volume and raise prices forever. The €550,000 electric Luce, the cut 2030 EV target, and the flat profit are small cracks in a multiple that prices flawlessness in perpetuity — and removes any margin of safety. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Prologis trades at 21x FFO while its rent-rollover engine has lost two-thirds of its thrust](2026-06-21T1700-prologis.md) · _2026-06-21_

Prologis raised guidance, posted record 64-million-square-foot leasing, pushed occupancy to 95.3%, and reported Q1 Core FFO of $1.50 — and near $128 the stock prices that supercycle story at roughly 21x FFO, a ~$132 billion structural e-commerce compounder. But the number that built the legend, the re-leasing spread, tells another story: net effective rent change on rollover ran 84% at the 3Q23 peak and just 31.9% in Q1 2026; cash rent change fell from 54% to 16.8%. The embedded lease mark-to-market has shrunk from roughly 60%-plus to about 17%. That gap is the organic growth engine, and it is emptying — with the same-store headline now leaning on unusually low bad debt and a development pivot into data centers, not the warehouse re-rating that minted the last decade. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [NextEra trades at a 22x growth premium while its financing canary cut payouts to zero](2026-06-21T1630-nextera-energy.md) · _2026-06-21_

NextEra beat again — $1.09 in adjusted Q1 earnings, up 10%, a record renewables backlog near 33 gigawatts, and a $221 billion balance sheet aimed at $40 billion of annual capital spending. The market pays roughly 22 times earnings, a premium to a utility sector near 20, on the premise that a regulated Florida monopoly bolted to the country's largest clean-energy developer is a secular growth machine rather than a leveraged, rate-sensitive, subsidy-fed construction company. This piece does not dispute the engineering; it asks why the company's own financing vehicle suspended its distribution to zero, rebranded from NextEra Energy Partners to XPLR Infrastructure, and bought back $3.7 billion of convertible obligations it could no longer roll. When the canary stops singing, you check the air. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [PDD's profit falls 15% as Temu's tariff cushion vanishes and the home-front subsidy war drains margins](2026-06-21T1600-pinduoduo.md) · _2026-06-21_

PDD Holdings — the Cayman-domiciled parent of Pinduoduo and Temu — reported Q1 2026 revenue of RMB106.2 billion (~US$14.6 billion), up 11%, the slowest growth in its public history. Net income fell 15% to RMB12.5 billion even as operating profit rose 22%, a contradiction resolved by below-the-line items propping up a model under a two-front assault. Abroad, the August 2025 end of the US de-minimis exemption removed the duty-free regime that made Temu's RMB-priced packages viable; at home, a subsidy war with Alibaba and JD.com drew a RMB528 million administrative fine in April 2026. These are structural and regulatory risks, not fraud, and the fine is a penalty, not proof of wrongdoing — but the market is pricing a price-war combatant as a compounder, through a VIE that owns contracts, not the company. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [ConocoPhillips earns less on more barrels as a $22.5B Marathon deal meets a $50 tape](2026-06-21T1530-conocophillips.md) · _2026-06-21_

ConocoPhillips wants to be owned as a through-cycle compounder — a low-cost machine that grows production, shrinks its share count, and returns ever-rising cash regardless of the oil price. Q1 2026 complicates that. Net income fell to $2.2 billion from $2.8 billion, adjusted EPS slipped to $1.89 from $2.09, and reported EPS dropped to $1.78 from $2.23 — all on roughly 4% more barrels, the gift of the all-stock, $22.5 billion Marathon Oil deal that closed in late 2024. Strip the acquired volumes and production was actually down about 1% pro-forma; realized price per barrel of oil equivalent fell to $50.36 from $53.34. The dividend held at $0.84 and the buyback ran $1 billion, but that is price-taker's math: when crude softens, the cash funding both comes straight out of the same barrel. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Applied Materials Trades at a Record 16x Sales While Its Biggest Market Shrinks](2026-06-21T1500-applied-materials.md) · _2026-06-21_

Applied Materials makes the machines that make the chips, and in the spring of 2026 the market decided those machines were a secular AI growth story rather than the most cyclical business in technology. The stock roughly tripled in a year, trading near a record sixteen times sales and around fifty-five times trailing earnings — multiples touched only a handful of times in forty years of booms and busts. Beneath the record-revenue headline sits a complicated ledger. The single largest geography, China, has collapsed from roughly forty percent of sales toward the mid-twenties, with management flagging a ~$600 million fiscal-2026 hit from export controls. And reported GAAP EPS of $3.51 exceeded the adjusted $2.86 — an inversion meaning a chunk of the headline profit came from marking up a Besi equity stake, not selling tools. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Sea Limited's revenue jumped 47% — but Shopee's profit fell while volume surged 30%](2026-06-21T1430-sea-limited.md) · _2026-06-21_

Sea Limited printed a triumphant Q1: $7.1 billion in revenue, up nearly 47%, its first billion-dollar adjusted-EBITDA quarter, and a stock that leapt double digits premarket. One layer down, the story inverts. The crown jewel, Shopee, saw segment adjusted EBITDA fall from $264.4 million to $223.2 million — down about 16% — even as merchandise volume rose 30% to a record $37.3 billion, the signature of a platform buying growth with logistics and VIP subsidies. The thesis is this Shopee segment-margin compression, not a Garena decline: Garena bookings actually rose ~20% to $931 million, and the critique there is that a hit-driven trough-bounce is being re-rated as a secular engine. Net income grew just 7% against 47% revenue growth, while a $9.9 billion consumer-credit book sits underneath. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Qualcomm's $238B Valuation Leans on a Royalty Toll Apple Is Walking Away From](2026-06-21T1400-qualcomm.md) · _2026-06-21_

Qualcomm prints $10.6 billion a quarter and a 72% margin on patents, but the engine behind that cash is a clock running down. Apple — one of three customers each worth 10% or more of revenue — plans Qualcomm modems in just 20% of iPhones in 2026 and none by 2027, a transition analysts size at a $7.3-to-$7.8-billion annual hole opening in 2028. The standalone quarter already shows the strain: total revenue down about 2% year over year, QCT handset revenue down 13%, non-GAAP operating margin compressed from roughly 34% to 31%, and Chinese Android shipments "meaningfully below" real demand. Management's answer is automotive and IoT — genuinely growing, genuinely smaller. The market still pays roughly 23 times earnings near a 52-week high for a franchise whose highest-margin dollar is a toll its biggest tenant is leaving. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Texas Instruments trades near 49x as a 90%-growth data-center sliver reprices the whole cycle](2026-06-21T1330-texas-instruments.md) · _2026-06-21_

Texas Instruments delivered the quarter the bulls wanted — Q1 2026 revenue of $4.83 billion, up 19% and ahead of guidance, EPS of $1.68 against a $1.36 consensus, gross margin back to 58%, net income up 31% to $1.55 billion, and a data-center line that exploded roughly 90% year over year — and the market answered by paying about 49 times trailing earnings for a maker of jelly-bean analog and embedded chips that historically changes hands near 24. That is the forensic problem in one sentence: a deeply cyclical industrial-and-automotive supplier re-rated as an AI-data-center secular grower on the strength of a segment still only eleven or twelve percent of revenue, while automotive — its largest historical end-market — sits flat-to-down with China softening into the back half. The numbers are real; the multiple is the bet. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Moody's hits records at 31x earnings on a toll booth that still bends to the bond cycle](2026-06-21T1300-moodys.md) · _2026-06-21_

Moody's just posted its best quarter ever — $2.1 billion in revenue, a record $1.2 billion ratings haul on more than $2 trillion of rated issuance, a 67% margin on the ratings engine, and adjusted EPS up 13% to $4.33. The market pays roughly 31 times trailing and 25 times forward for half a regulatory ratings duopoly issuers cannot legally route around, and that moat is real. The forensic question is how much of the record is structural and how much is a refinancing wave cresting right now. Strip the once-in-a-cycle $2 trillion issuance quarter, weigh the gap between $4.33 adjusted and $3.73 GAAP (mostly acquired-intangible amortization), and watch generative AI lap at the analytics moat — and a secular multiple starts to look like a bet that the debt cycle has been abolished. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Nu Holdings clears $5B revenue and $871M profit — and its credit book is seasoning faster than the bulls admit](2026-06-21T1230-nu-holdings.md) · _2026-06-21_

Nu Holdings posted the best first quarter in its history: revenue past $5 billion, $871 million in net income, 135 million customers, Mexico at break-even ahead of plan, and a 30%-plus ROE priced at a premium to every legacy Latin American bank. But on its own disclosed figures a more cyclical machine appears: the credit-loss allowance jumped 33% in a single quarter to nearly $1.8 billion, the early-stage 15–90 day delinquency bucket leapt from 4.1% to 5.0%, risk-adjusted net interest margin gave back a full 100 basis points, and an unsecured loan book grew 53% into a Brazilian Selic rate still near 14%. Nu is deliberately steering customers toward higher-loss products to lift revenue per user — a choice whose true cost only shows once the vintages season. This is analysis of the company's own numbers, not any allegation of wrongdoing. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [KKR posts record $758B AUM and $1.13 fee earnings — but $0.41 GAAP profit tells the real story](2026-06-21T1200-kkr.md) · _2026-06-21_

KKR closed Q1 2026 with the loudest headline in alternatives: record $758 billion AUM, management fees up roughly 30% to $1.19 billion, fee-related earnings of $1.13 per share, total operating earnings of $1.47. The market is invited to price the firm on that capital-light annuity. But one column over, GAAP net income was just $364.8 million — basic EPS of $0.41 — because the insurance arm absorbed $652.7 million of net investment-related losses and the asset-management book lost another $316.4 million. Realized carried interest, the supposed payoff for patient capital, came to $197.2 million while $10.2 billion of carry sits unrealized, frozen in a slow-exit market that pushed management's own 2026 earnings target below $7 a share. This is a story about which number is real. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Schwab's Record Quarter Quietly Bet Its Margin on the Fed Never Cutting Again](2026-06-21T1130-charles-schwab.md) · _2026-06-21_

Charles Schwab printed the cleanest quarter of its post-pandemic life — net revenue up 16% to $6.48 billion, GAAP profit up 30% to $2.48 billion, net interest margin clawing back to 2.88% from 2.53%, and the high-cost supplemental funding that nearly broke the equity story in 2023 paid down 77% to roughly $5.1 billion. Management now tracks above its own $5.70–$5.80 EPS scenario. But read the fine print: the margin recovery is explicitly underwritten by a forward curve pricing in no 2026 rate cuts — the CFO said the firm benefits from a "lack of rate cuts." A company that nearly drowned when rates rose in 2023 is now quietly priced for rates to stay up forever. The bond book is still underwater, the capital cushion sits at its self-imposed floor, and the stock fell on the record print. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [MercadoLibre's revenue roared 49% in Q1 — so why did operating profit just fall 20%?](2026-06-21T1100-mercadolibre.md) · _2026-06-21_

MercadoLibre booked $8.85 billion of net revenue in Q1 2026, a 49% leap and its fastest growth since 2022 — yet on its own income statement operating income fell 20% to $611 million, the operating margin collapsed nearly 600 basis points to 6.9%, EPS of $8.23 missed by double digits, and the engine doing the spending is a credit book that ballooned 87% in twelve months to $14.6 billion. MELI is not buying warehouses with that money; it is buying loans, and in lending, revenue is booked immediately while losses are provisioned over time. Management itself tied the margin compression to richer credit-card mix and higher Brazilian provisions, with NIMAL falling to 17.8% from 22.7%. The point is built on MELI's own disclosed figures — rising provisions and margin compression — not any allegation of wrongdoing. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Progressive's Record 82 Combined Ratio Is a Cycle Peak Wearing a Secular Mask](2026-06-21T1030-progressive.md) · _2026-06-21_

Progressive printed an 82.1 combined ratio for May 2026 and a 36% jump in monthly profit to $1.45 billion — the kind of underwriting margin that, in a normal world, lasts about as long as a Florida summer. The bull case calls it a durable machine; the forensic reading is colder. Auto insurance is cyclical, regulated and mean-reverting, and Progressive's golden eighteen months were manufactured by a once-in-a-generation hard-pricing cycle — double-digit rate hikes layered through 2023–24 that earned in just as accident-year severity cooled. That tide is now turning: Progressive is already handing nearly a billion dollars back to Florida drivers, and the state's top insurers are filing average rate cuts near 8%. A multiple that capitalizes an 80s combined ratio as the new normal is paying secular money for a cyclical peak. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Pfizer's 6% dividend leans on a $43B oncology bet and a GAAP payout near 130%](2026-06-21T1000-pfizer.md) · _2026-06-21_

Pfizer printed a clean beat — $14.45 billion in Q1 2026 revenue, up 5.4%, adjusted EPS of $0.75 topping consensus, full-year guidance reaffirmed. Read the headline and the COVID hangover looks over. Read the cash-flow statement and a darker story emerges: $9.77 billion in dividends paid against roughly $9.08 billion of free cash flow last year, a GAAP payout ratio that vaulted toward 126%, total debt climbing to about $67 billion as liquid assets thinned to $13.6 billion, and a $7.7 billion cost program doing more for EPS than any new molecule. Pfizer spent its pandemic windfall buying a future — Seagen for $43 billion, Metsera, Biohaven — and now must out-run a patent cliff that hits Eliquis and Ibrance before the bought growth fully arrives. The dividend is the tell; the pipeline is the wager. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [FEMSA's 97% profit surge is mostly an accounting mirage — strip it and earnings fell 36%](2026-06-21T0930-femsa.md) · _2026-06-21_

FEMSA's Q1 2026 headline read like a triumph: net consolidated income up 97.3% to Ps. 17,639 million, total revenue up 6.1%, the stock popping 5.6% on the day. But the forensic story sits in the footnote. Pull out the one-time gain from the BradyPLUS–Imperial Dade transaction and the underlying number collapses — net income excluding that gain fell 36.4% to Ps. 5,688 million, sandbagged by higher net financing expenses and the disappearance of discontinued-operations income that flattered the year-ago base. This is a tale of two FEMSAs: a genuinely excellent Oxxo convenience engine compounding at 20.9% operating-income growth, bolted to a flat Coca-Cola FEMSA bottler whose operating income actually shrank, the whole apparatus geared to a peso-sensitive, remittance-dependent Mexican consumer exposed to US–Mexico tariff and political risk. The headline is real; the quality of it is not. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Intuitive Surgical's 23% growth is real — but a 40x multiple is buying a monopoly the FDA just ended](2026-06-21T0900-intuitive-surgical.md) · _2026-06-21_

Intuitive Surgical printed a flawless first quarter — $2.77 billion in revenue, up 23%, da Vinci procedures up 16%, an installed base of 11,395 systems compounding razor-and-blades cash like clockwork. The annuity is genuine and the franchise is one of the best in medtech. But the stock trades near 40 times forward earnings and roughly 18 times revenue precisely because the market has priced two decades of monopoly into perpetuity — and in December 2025 the FDA cleared Medtronic's Hugo for U.S. urology, the first soft-tissue robotic rival in twenty-plus years, with J&J's Ottava de novo request filed in January 2026. Layer on a 100-basis-point tariff drag baked into 2026 gross-margin guidance and a da Vinci 5 transition still ramping, and this is a great business wearing a price tag that requires perfection it can no longer fully control. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Medtronic's "Best Growth in a Decade" Was Mostly Currency, and Constant-Currency EPS Fell 2%](2026-06-21T0830-medtronic.md) · _2026-06-21_

Medtronic is the largest pure-play medical-device maker on earth, and on June 3, 2026 it told the world it had delivered its highest annual revenue growth in ten years — $36.4 billion, up 8.4%. It is a true statement and a flattering frame, and the gap between the two is the whole story. Strip out a favorable $824 million currency swing and organic growth was 5.8%; strip currency from the bottom line and adjusted EPS actually fell 2% on the year. The $5.53 of adjusted EPS the company leads with sits $1.80 above the $3.73 it earned under GAAP. Two of its four segments grew about 3% organically, and it carved out MiniMed in a March IPO that floated only 10% — leaving Medtronic owning roughly 90% and still consolidating the unit's growth into the very organic rate the spin was meant to flatter. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [General Motors' record EPS is engineered by a shrinking share count, not a growing business](2026-06-20T1800-general-motors.md) · _2026-06-20_

GM's Q1 2026 looked like a blowout — adjusted EPS of $3.70 beating consensus by more than 40% and a raised full-year range of $11.50–$13.50 — but the quarter is mostly arithmetic. Revenue actually fell to $43.6 billion from $44.0 billion, a 1.5-point margin tailwind came from a one-off Supreme Court IEEPA tariff true-up (~$500 million), and GM booked another $1.1 billion of EV restructuring charges on top of roughly $7 billion in earlier China and Cruise write-downs. The per-share growth rests on a share count cut more than 40% since 2015. Strip the buyback and the tariff windfall and the underlying business is a flat-to-down cyclical truck-and-SUV franchise priced as if the turnaround were structural. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Rio Tinto's $25 billion EBITDA still rides one rock — and China is letting go](2026-06-20T1730-rio-tinto.md) · _2026-06-20_

Rio Tinto markets itself as a diversified energy-transition house — copper, Arcadium lithium, Simandou, aluminium — but the cash machine is still iron ore sold to one customer: China's steel mills. FY2025 delivered $57.6 billion revenue, $25.4 billion underlying EBITDA and a $6.5 billion dividend at a 60% payout, yet Pilbara shipments actually fell 1% and the gains came from price and cost-out, not volume. Now the tape is turning: Chinese steel output is down ~5% year-on-year, property investment fell 16.2%, consensus iron-ore prices are set to slide from ~$101 to ~$94 a tonne, and Rio's own Simandou is about to pour ~20 million tonnes of new supply into a softening market — depressing the price of its own core product. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Royal Caribbean rides record bookings into a $22 billion debt headwind it can't out-sail](2026-06-20T1700-royal-caribbean.md) · _2026-06-20_

Royal Caribbean's Q1 2026 was a genuine beat — revenue up 11.3% to $4.45 billion, adjusted EPS of $3.60, ships above 100% occupancy, $1.1 billion returned to shareholders — and the stock jumped 7% to near $312. Yet in the same release management cut full-year adjusted EPS guidance to a $17.30 midpoint, citing a $0.74 fuel headwind and softening Mediterranean bookings after late-quarter geopolitical shocks. Beneath the celebration sits $22 billion of gross debt, a 2.2x debt-to-equity ratio in the sector's bottom decile, and a seven-ship Icon-class building spree through 2030. The valuation isn't stretched; the risk is that a peak-cycle E, cheap fuel and a calm map are priced as permanent for a 100%-discretionary operator that controls none of them. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Marriott trades at 31x forward earnings while its core US RevPAR grows just 4%](2026-06-20T1630-marriott.md) · _2026-06-20_

Marriott is the market's favorite kind of stock: an asset-light fee-and-loyalty compounder priced at roughly 31 times forward earnings, above its own ten-year average. But strip Q1 2026 down to its load-bearing organic number and it is more cyclical than secular — worldwide RevPAR rose 4.2% in constant dollars, U.S. & Canada just 4.0%, and full-year guidance decelerates to 2%–3%. The headline 17% adjusted-EPS growth is manufactured downstream by 4.5% net-unit growth, a co-branded credit-card royalty step-up, and an aggressive levered buyback (~$0.7 billion in the quarter, $4.4 billion planned for 2026). A $17 billion net-debt position and a ~29-cent adjusted-versus-GAAP EPS wedge underline that a late-cycle traveler is paying a peak multiple for a peaking cycle. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Shell's $3B buyback is borrowing against a trading windfall it can't repeat](2026-06-20T1600-shell.md) · _2026-06-20_

Shell printed $6.9 billion of adjusted earnings in Q1 2026, up 24% year over year, and rewarded shareholders with a fresh $3 billion buyback and a 5% dividend hike. But the engine behind the surprise was its most cyclical, least repeatable line: trading and refining margins that swung Chemicals & Products to $1.93 billion and lifted Marketing, while the crown-jewel Integrated Gas/LNG franchise actually fell 27% year over year. Meanwhile net debt climbed to $52.6 billion, gearing rose to 23.2%, and operating cash flow fell roughly a third. Distributions of $5.3 billion exceeded $2.9 billion of free cash flow by about 1.8x — the gap funded mechanically by the balance sheet. The buyback is real; the question is whether it is paid from durable income or from leverage. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Darden's 4.2% comp is 3.5% price: a pricing engine wearing a traffic suit](2026-06-20T1530-darden.md) · _2026-06-20_

Darden's fiscal-2026 third quarter posted a blended same-restaurant sales gain of 4.2%, which Wall Street read as Olive Garden and LongHorn rediscovering growth. Decompose it and roughly 3.5 points were check (menu price) plus ~0.1 of mix, leaving traffic as a rounding error. Olive Garden's flagship +3.2% comp rests on only ~100 basis points of traffic that itself leaned on a 130-basis-point catering tailwind — meaning underlying dine-in traffic was negative — with lighter-portion mix and delivery fees clawing back the rest. The 5.9% total-sales gain is further inflated by 31 net new boxes and the absorbed Chuy's roll-up. At ~22 times earnings and a $24 billion market value, the stock is priced as if that price-led, borrowed traffic were secular. It is neither. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Estée Lauder priced at 26x forward earnings on a 2% organic turn it can't yet bank](2026-06-20T1500-estee-lauder.md) · _2026-06-20_

Estée Lauder told a triumphant turnaround story on May 1, 2026 — organic sales back to growth, China gaining share, Hainan accelerating, fragrance double-digit, guidance raised — and the stock surged to near $87, roughly 26 times forward earnings and more than 80% above the staples median. But the quarter's growth was just 2% organic, and the GAAP page is colder: net income of $89 million on $3.71 billion of sales, a 6.7% GAAP operating margin against a 15.0% adjusted one, an eight-point wedge. GAAP EPS was $0.24 versus $0.91 adjusted. The dividend has already been cut ~47%, and a restructuring now slated at up to $1.7 billion and as many as 10,000 jobs is still running, with most savings landing only in fiscal 2027. The turn has barely begun. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [AstraZeneca's 16% oncology engine is real — its 28% GAAP margin and a Beijing courtroom are the tax nobody prices](2026-06-20T1430-astrazeneca.md) · _2026-06-20_

AstraZeneca closed Q1 2026 with $15.29 billion of revenue, up 8% at constant currency, and an oncology franchise that grew 16% to $6.8 billion and now supplies 44% of the top line — letting management reconfirm low-double-digit core-EPS growth and the $80 billion-by-2030 ambition. The slide the bulls skip is the reconciliation: core EPS of $2.58 sits ~30% above reported GAAP EPS of $1.99, and the 35% core operating margin shrinks to a 28% reported margin once amortization, impairments and restructuring are counted. Beneath it, a China business of $1.92 billion crept just 2% at constant currency while a former country chief faces charges/indictments on data, illegal-trade and insurance-fraud matters — alleged, not adjudicated or convicted. A great drug company wears a flawless-execution price tag over a contested geography and an adjusted-earnings gap. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Constellation Brands' beer engine just stalled to +1% as Modelo and Corona shrink](2026-06-20T1400-constellation-brands.md) · _2026-06-20_

Constellation sells itself as the one beer company that grows while America drinks less — and for a decade that was true. The fiscal 2026 numbers, for the year ended February 28, say the engine is sputtering. Consolidated net sales fell ~10% to $9.14 billion, wine and spirits collapsed 58% as the segment was sold for parts, and beer grew net sales just 1% in the fourth quarter and fell 3% for the full year to $8.32 billion, with shipments down 3.8% and depletions down 2.1%. Worse, the two brands the whole bull case rests on are declining — Modelo Especial depletions off ~3%, Corona Extra ~7% — with growth backfilled by far smaller labels. Q4 operating margin fell 340 basis points to 33.2%, beer-margin guidance was cut, and full-year beer revenue is guided to a flat −1% to +1% band. A single-engine plane losing altitude. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Kraft Heinz pays a 6.6% dividend on shrinking volumes and a $9.3 billion confession](2026-06-20T1330-kraft-heinz.md) · _2026-06-20_

Kraft Heinz delivered a quarter that reads like a confession. Q1 2026 net sales rose a token 0.8% to ~$6.05 billion, but organic net sales fell 0.4% as volume and mix dropped 1.2 points while pricing added back only 0.8 — the 3G zero-based-budgeting machine running in reverse, with a consumer that has finally stopped paying up. Full-year guidance concedes the math: organic sales down 1.5% to 3.5% and constant-currency adjusted operating income down 14% to 18%. Behind it sits a 2025 in which a $9.3 billion impairment — over $6 billion of it goodwill — drove a ~$4.7 billion net loss, and a ~6.6% dividend resting on a balance sheet padded with roughly $22 billion of goodwill and other soft assets. This is what a value trap looks like mid-spring. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [TJX beats, raises, and still leaves no margin for error at 34 times earnings](2026-06-20T1300-tjx.md) · _2026-06-20_

TJX printed a near-flawless first quarter — net sales of $14.3 billion up 9%, consolidated comps up 6%, pretax margin of 12.0% up a full 1.7 points, diluted EPS of $1.19 up 29% — and management raised every line of full-year guidance. So why is it a forensic story rather than a victory lap? Because the same release that boasts 6% comps tells you, in the company's own raised numbers, that it expects the rest of the year to run at just 3% to 4% — a deceleration management forecasts, not one a bear invented. The stock trades near 34 times forward earnings, more than double the cyclical-retail median, on a pretax margin already at an all-time-high ceiling after a once-in-a-generation trade-down wave. The operator is elite; the question is what 34x actually buys, and what happens to the multiple if a single ordinary quarter merely meets the plan. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Sony's record ¥1.45 trillion profit hides a console past its peak and a ¥208 billion write-off year](2026-06-20T1230-sony.md) · _2026-06-20_

Sony closed fiscal 2025 with the headline investors wanted — record sales of ¥12.48 trillion and record operating income of ¥1.45 trillion, up 13% — and the market filed it under "content compounder," the durable IP machine that owns Spider-Man, catalog rights and the PlayStation network. Beneath the trophy the picture turns cyclical fast: PS5 shipped just 2.8 million units in the closing quarter versus 9.5 million the quarter before, lifetime volume of 93.7 million sits on the back half of a console curve, image sensors ride the smartphone replacement cycle, and the "record" profit absorbed roughly ¥208 billion of impairments — a ¥120.1 billion Bungie write-down and ¥44.9 billion of EV-exit losses among them. Sony spun its financial arm out in October 2025 and reclassified it as discontinued, reshaping the denominator just as the growth segments turn. The compounder narrative is real; the cyclicality it papers over is more real. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Home Depot grows sales 4.8% but earnings fall, comps barely move, and the stock still prices a housing thaw](2026-06-20T1200-home-depot.md) · _2026-06-20_

Home Depot reported $41.8 billion in first-quarter fiscal 2026 sales on May 19, up 4.8% — but the engine underneath is stalled. Comparable sales rose just 0.6%, U.S. comps a thinner 0.4%, and roughly 55 basis points of even that came from foreign exchange, not from a single additional contractor. The growth that pushed the top line was bought: the GMS acquisition, folded into the SRS Distribution arm, added about $1.3 billion of net sales the prior-year base never contained. Meanwhile earnings actually fell — GAAP diluted EPS slid to $3.30 from $3.45, adjusted EPS to $3.43 from $3.56 — operating margin compressed roughly a full point, and the company now carries about $44.8 billion of long-term debt with net interest expense guided near $2.3 billion. The CEO's own words: demand was "relatively similar to fiscal 2025." Yet the stock trades north of 22 times forward earnings, a multiple that only works if a rate-driven remodel recovery management cannot point to arrives on schedule. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Ulta Beauty Beat With 5.3% Comps — Then Guided the Rest of the Year to Half That](2026-06-20T1130-ulta-beauty.md) · _2026-06-20_

Ulta Beauty did the hard thing a retailer is supposed to do: it beat. First-quarter fiscal 2026 net sales rose 11.1% to roughly $3.16 billion, comparable sales climbed 5.3%, operating income grew 11.6% to $448.3 million, and diluted EPS jumped 15.5% to $7.74 — all ahead of Wall Street, and management nudged its profit outlook higher. The stock is rich, the loyalty program enormous, the balance sheet clean. And yet buried in the same release is a number the celebration skips: for the full fiscal year, Ulta reaffirmed comparable-sales guidance of just 2.5% to 3.5% — less than half the pace it just posted. Management is telling you, in its own filing, that the quarter you are applauding is not the run-rate. This is a piece about the gap between a beat and a guide, about an operating margin that has fallen from roughly 16% at its 2022 peak toward 12%, about competitors moving onto Ulta's turf, and about a stock priced for a category that already had its boom. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Toyota posts record revenue and a North American loss — the math that record obscures](2026-06-20T1100-toyota.md) · _2026-06-20_

This is not a record-profit story. Toyota's fiscal 2026, reported May 8, 2026, is a study in the gap between a top line and a bottom one: net revenue hit a record 50.684 trillion yen, up 5.5%, yet operating income fell 21.5% to 3.8 trillion yen, net income attributable to Toyota dropped roughly 19% to about $25.7 billion, and North America — the firm's profit stronghold — swung to a $1.9 billion operating loss, its first regional loss in sixteen years. U.S. tariffs carved out 1.38 trillion yen of operating profit; unfavorable currency stripped another $13.5 billion from earnings. The same weak yen that flattered Toyota's "record profit" headlines for three straight years has reversed, and management's own FY2027 guidance — operating income cut again to 3.0 trillion yen — concedes the squeeze is not over. The market is being asked to price a tariff-and-currency-battered trough as if hybrids alone make it durable. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [FedEx's $5.25 adjusted EPS is a cost-cut mirage over a stalling freight economy](2026-06-20T1030-fedex.md) · _2026-06-20_

FedEx beat its fiscal third quarter on March 19, 2026, printing $24 billion in revenue and a roughly 16 percent adjusted-EPS jump to $5.25 from $4.51 — and the stock leapt nearly 9 percent after hours on a self-help narrative that has carried the equity for two years. Underneath, the picture inverts: GAAP earnings were $4.41, the operating margin 5.6 percent, the freight division that anchored the franchise saw revenue fall 4.7 percent on a 4.8 percent tonnage decline, and the company is replacing a lost $2 billion-a-year USPS air contract while Amazon builds the largest parcel network in America. The DRIVE and Network 2.0 cost programs are real, but they subtract expense from a top line whose underlying B2B demand is shrinking. On June 1, FedEx hived off its freight unit into FedEx Freight Corporation, paying the parent $4.1 billion of debt-funded cash on the way out. This is a freight-recession cyclical wearing the costume of a secular compounder — and the gap between $5.25 and $4.41 is where the costume is stitched. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Union Pacific Grew Revenue 3% While Carloads Fell — and Now Bets the Story on an $85 Billion Merger](2026-06-20T1000-union-pacific.md) · _2026-06-20_

Union Pacific posted record first-quarter 2026 results — operating revenue of $6.2 billion, up 3%, a reported operating ratio of 60.5%, net income of $1.7 billion, and adjusted diluted EPS of $2.93, up high-single-digits from $2.70 — and presented it as proof of a machine running better than ever. Read one layer down and a different picture surfaces: total carloads fell 1% year over year, the volume engine that should power a freight railroad ran in reverse, and the entire 3% revenue gain came from core pricing, fuel surcharge, and business mix rather than from moving more stuff. That is the signature of a business converting pricing power and operating-ratio discipline into earnings while its physical franchise stays flat-to-down. Layered on top is the $85 billion proposed acquisition of Norfolk Southern — a transcontinental merger shareholders have approved, regulators have only conditionally accepted, and that now carries a Surface Transportation Board review running into 2027. This is a story about how much of UP's future is already promised and how little is yet earned. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [SAP's 27% Cloud Headline Hides 6% Reported Growth and a 13-Point Currency Crutch](2026-06-20T0930-sap.md) · _2026-06-20_

SAP sells itself to investors as a German hyperscaler in waiting — Business AI, the Joule copilot, a cloud backlog vaulting 25% and a Cloud ERP Suite compounding at 30%. Strip the constant-currency lacquer off those numbers and a quieter machine appears. The same quarter that produced a 27% cloud-growth headline produced total revenue up just 6% as actually reported, in the euros SAP actually banks; the gap is a thirteen-point currency adjustment that flatters every cloud line in the deck. The current cloud backlog SAP leans on is already telegraphed by its own CFO to decelerate "over the coming quarters." The growth is real, but it is bought-forward growth — migrations of an existing ECC license base onto RISE contracts, re-papered and re-counted as net-new cloud. And the market has noticed: the ADR is down roughly 41% over six months, near a 52-week low while management insists the secular story is intact. This is the anatomy of a re-rating that hasn't finished re-rating. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Eaton trades near 30x on a data-center backlog the cycle has not yet paid out](2026-06-20T0900-eaton.md) · _2026-06-20_

Eaton just printed its best quarter in a century of existence — $7.5 billion in record sales, 10% organic growth, data-center orders up a vertiginous 240%, and a 2026 organic-growth guide lifted to roughly 10% from 8% at the midpoint — and the market has rewarded the moment with a forward multiple north of 30, more than half again the industrial-products median near 21. That is the entire trade in one sentence: a 114-year-old maker of breakers, transformers, switchgear and busways, historically a faithful proxy for the industrial cycle, is now priced as a structural, secular, AI-electrification compounder whose backlog never empties. The forensic question is not whether the orders are real — they are — but whether a record book of business, built at the apex of a reshoring-plus-utility-plus-hyperscaler capex wave, is being capitalized as permanent demand at exactly the multiple that leaves no margin for the wave to recede. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Caterpillar near $975 at 42x earnings, pricing a data-center engine boom as if the machinery cycle had been repealed](2026-06-20T0830-caterpillar.md) · _2026-06-20_

Caterpillar trades at a record near $975 and a trailing P/E above 42 — roughly double its decade-long average — on the strength of a quarter that looked, on the surface, like vindication: revenue up 22% to $17.4 billion, adjusted EPS of $5.54, and a backlog swollen to a record $63 billion. Look underneath and the story narrows. The growth is concentrated in reciprocating engines sold into data centers, a single demand wave the company itself won't deploy capacity against until 2027–2029. Operating margin slipped to 17.7% from 18.1%, Resource Industries profit collapsed 39%, tariffs are eating $2.2–$2.4 billion this year, and a $1.5 billion dealer-inventory build flattered Construction. This is a late-cycle, price-taking heavy-machinery maker being valued like a secular compounder — cyclical earnings dressed as an AI annuity, with the multiple, not the machines, doing the work. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Chewy's growth slides to 7.7% as guidance cut sends shares to a new floor](2026-06-18T1800-chewy.md) · _2026-06-18_

Chewy just printed its strongest profit quarter ever — $94.8 million of GAAP net income — and the stock fell anyway, because the only number the market cared about was the one management trimmed. Net sales grew 7.7% in the quarter ended May 3, 2026, decelerating from 8.3% a year earlier, and full-year revenue guidance was cut to $13.40–$13.55 billion, with management conceding net customer adds would drift to the low end of their range "given the current environment." Active customers crept up just 3.6% to 21.5 million; the growth is being extracted from a near-flat loyal cohort (net sales per customer up ~4.6% to $597), not new households. It is a margin story dressed as a growth story — record profit flattered by a $73.4 million stock-based-comp line — still carrying a trailing P/E near 49 while sitting 45% below its high. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Waste Management trades at 31x earnings while 2026 growth rides almost entirely on price, not volume](2026-06-18T1730-waste-management.md) · _2026-06-18_

Waste Management is the bond-proxy industrial America loves to own — a recession-proof toll on the garbage every household must throw away. But the Q1 2026 numbers expose what the premium is paying for. Operating revenue of $6.227 billion missed the $6.287 billion consensus even as adjusted EPS of $1.81 beat $1.70 — a tell the beat came from margin and buybacks, not the top line. The 2026 guidance is starker still: core price of 5.4%–5.8% against volume of just 0.2%–0.6%, raising prices roughly ten times faster than it moves more trash. Layer on a $7.2 billion Stericycle acquisition that pushed leverage toward 3.6x and a trailing P/E near 31 — about half again the waste-industry median near 20 — and you have a defensive compounder priced for an offensive decade. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Sherwin-Williams sells $5.67B of paint, admits no recovery is coming, and trades like one already arrived](2026-06-18T1700-sherwin-williams.md) · _2026-06-18_

Sherwin-Williams posted 6.8% revenue growth in Q1 2026 ($5.67 billion) and the market called it strength — but pull the receipt apart and the growth is bought, not built: an October 2025 Brazilian acquisition called Suvinil, favorable currency translation, and a price list that keeps climbing while the gallons barely move. Same-store sales in the flagship Paint Stores Group rose 2.4% on pricing, not volume; the Consumer Brands DIY business shrank as North American demand fell again. Management's own words were the tell — they expect "little to no recovery in most end markets this year." Yet the stock trades around 25 to 31 times forward earnings, a fat premium to a chemicals-industry median near 20, as if a housing-led volume reacceleration were a certainty rather than a hope management has explicitly disowned. A cyclical priced as a secular compounder. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Carrier's data-center cooling story masks a 1% organic decline and a 44x multiple](2026-06-18T1630-carrier.md) · _2026-06-18_

Carrier Global printed $5.341 billion of Q1 2026 revenue and let one number do the talking: data-center orders up 500%, with a backlog that already covers the full $1.5 billion data-center sales target for the year. The order book is genuinely real — orders up 500%, the backlog covering the target — and the article concedes that plainly. But the same quarter delivered organic revenue down about 1%, GAAP diluted EPS of just $0.28 against an adjusted $0.57, an operating margin that collapsed to 4.8% from 12.1%, free cash flow of negative $15 million, and residential sales down roughly 12%. This is a housing-cyclical, China-exposed equipment maker trading near 44 times earnings on roughly 7% data-center revenue — the re-rating a bet that demonstration becomes deployment before the cycle turns. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Nutrien's record quarter is a potash-price bet dressed as a food-security story](2026-06-18T1600-nutrien.md) · _2026-06-18_

Nutrien booked $6.0 billion of Q1 2026 revenue and called it a record, riding record potash volumes of 3.51 million tonnes and a 21% jump in realized potash prices to $264 a tonne — yet the GAAP line tells a quieter tale: $139 million of net earnings, $0.27 a share, less than half the $0.51 the company prefers you remember. Strip the adjustments and you find a capital-heavy commodity producer whose fortunes rise and fall with benchmarks it does not set. Nitrogen EBITDA grew on a 13% price rise even as volumes fell 5% — earnings tracked the benchmark, not the company. The same potash that fetched $1,202 a tonne in April 2022 now changes hands near $310. The bull narrative calls this a secular food-security franchise; the tape calls it a price-taker that caught an up-cycle — and the stock fell roughly 7% the day it printed its "record." Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Deere trades near record highs on trough earnings as its core farm engine shrinks 14%](2026-06-18T1530-deere.md) · _2026-06-18_

Deere just told investors fiscal 2026 will earn roughly half of what it earned at the 2023 peak — net income guided to $4.5–5.0 billion against $10.166 billion three years ago — and the stock responded by sitting within striking distance of its all-time high. The headline was that second-quarter revenue grew 5% and profit fell only 2%, a picture of resilience. Look one layer down and it evaporates: Production and Precision Agriculture, the high-margin core that is the actual John Deere, saw sales fall 14% and operating margin collapse from 22.0% to 15.7%. Lower-margin construction equipment and lawn tractors filled the hole. The market is paying a peak multiple — north of 32 times trailing earnings — for trough, cyclical earnings management itself calls the bottom of the cycle, pricing the recovery as if it were already booked. Cyclical earnings dressed as secular compounding. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Knight-Swift Earned Nine Cents and Lost Money on GAAP — But the Stock Prices a Full Recovery](2026-06-18T1500-knight-swift.md) · _2026-06-18_

Knight-Swift is North America's largest truckload carrier, and in Q1 2026 it earned an adjusted nine cents a share — down from twenty-eight a year earlier — while posting a GAAP loss of a penny, swinging from a nineteen-cent profit. Management blames roughly $45 million of one-time items: an unfavorable LTL arbitration award, a Mexican VAT dispute, deferred warehousing, winter weather, and a fuel spike. The consolidated adjusted operating ratio worsened to 97%, and the less-than-truckload unit swung to an operating loss. Yet the shares trade as though the freight recession is a memory, the bull case resting almost entirely on a "this is the trough, the up-cycle is next" narrative the company has been telling investors, in some form, for the better part of three years. A cyclical priced as a secular compounder at the precise moment its own numbers say the cycle has not yet turned. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Fastenal grows 12% into a soft factory floor — at 35x, the math leaves no room to miss](2026-06-18T1430-fastenal.md) · _2026-06-18_

Fastenal printed a clean quarter on April 13: net sales of $2,201.7 million, up 12.4% on a daily basis, diluted EPS of $0.30, operating margin nudged to 20.3%. The market shrugged and the stock fell, because the disappointment was never in the revenue line — it was in the gross margin, which slid 50 basis points to 44.6% as tariff-driven cost rose faster than Fastenal could price. The forensic problem: a company whose top line is mechanically chained to the U.S. manufacturing cycle — a PMI that spent most of last year flirting with contraction — is valued at roughly 35 times forward earnings, nearly double the 18–19x its distribution peers fetch. That is a secular multiple bolted onto a cyclical body. The growth is real and the moat genuine, but at this price the stock has pre-spent every share gain and every month the factory PMI stays above 50. Perfection is in the quote; the cycle is not. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Pool Corp's $5.3B revenue is flat for a third year while new-pool builds sit 40% below their peak](2026-06-18T1400-pool-corp.md) · _2026-06-18_

Pool Corporation calls itself the indispensable plumbing of an 11-million-pool installed base, and on the maintenance layer that claim is fair: chemicals and replacement parts flow whether or not a homeowner finances a new backyard. But the company built its pandemic-era growth — and its premium multiple — on a new-construction wave that has now declined for four consecutive years, with roughly 58,000–60,000 in-ground pools built in the United States in 2025 versus nearly 98,000 at the 2022 peak, a drop on the order of 40%. Net sales have been pinned near $5.3 billion since 2023; 2025 earnings per share fell about 4% to $10.85 as operating income slipped. Management frames the maintenance floor as durability and the discretionary trough as a coiled spring. The forensic question is whether a distributor whose growth engine has stalled for three years deserves a secular-compounder multiple, or whether the floor is simply the floor. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Rollins Trades Near 50 Times Earnings on 6.6% Organic Growth as Bought Deals Pad the Topline](2026-06-18T1330-rollins.md) · _2026-06-18_

Rollins is one of the most beloved defensive compounders on the American market — the parent of Orkin, a pest-control machine whose customers pay every quarter to keep ants, termites, and rodents out, and whose stock has crushed the index for decades on recurring revenue. It is a genuinely excellent business, and nothing here disputes that. But it now trades near 50 times trailing earnings — a multiple that belongs on asset-light secular software, not on a route-density services roll-up whose underlying engine grows in the mid-single digits and whose double-digit topline is increasingly assembled by buying smaller competitors. In Q1 2026, reported on April 23, revenue rose 10.2% to $906.4 million, but organic growth was just 6.6% and GAAP earnings per share were flat at $0.22 against an adjusted $0.24. This is what happens when a wonderful, slow-growing, acquisition-fed compounder is priced for permanent perfection. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Cintas Trades at 36 Times Earnings on 8% Growth as It Bets $5.5 Billion on UniFirst](2026-06-18T1300-cintas.md) · _2026-06-18_

Cintas is a genuinely superb uniform-rental and facility-services compounder — a record 51.0% gross margin in fiscal Q3 2026, 45 straight years of dividend increases, and decades of crushing the S&P 500. None of that is in dispute. The forensic problem is the price: at roughly 36 times trailing earnings, the market pays a software-style multiple for a business whose revenue is structurally indexed to employment and business formation. Organic growth has decelerated to a healthy-but-not-double-digit 8.2%, EPS rose 9.7% against 8.4% net-income growth (buybacks doing part of the work), and management is now pinning the next leg on a roughly $5.5 billion acquisition of rival UniFirst — bought growth layered atop an organic slowdown, with the record margin extrapolated as a baseline. Priced for permanent perfection. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Generac's home-resilience engine is flat; a data-center bet now carries an 89% rally](2026-06-18T1230-generac.md) · _2026-06-18_

Generac sells itself as the secular play on energy resilience — a failing grid, a homeowner wiring in backup power, recurring climate anxiety converting to recurring sales. The Q1 2026 numbers tell a quieter story. Consolidated revenue rose 12% to $1.06 billion and the stock has run roughly 90% in a year, but the Residential franchise that anchors the entire secular thesis grew just 1% to about $549 million, with home-standby unit volumes actually falling and price the only thing holding the line. Energy storage shrank. Every dollar of acceleration came from the Commercial & Industrial segment, up 28% on data-center backlog. The risk is not that Generac is failing — it isn't — but that investors are paying a resilience multiple for a company whose resilience business has stalled, while its growth rides a second cyclical bet, hyperscale capex, dressed in the same secular costume. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Conagra's Earnings Fell 23% as a Held Dividend Strains a $7.3 Billion Balance Sheet](2026-06-18T1200-conagra.md) · _2026-06-18_

Conagra is the kind of packaged-food name income investors are supposed to fall asleep holding — Birds Eye, Marie Callender's, Slim Jim, Duncan Hines — and its fiscal Q3 2026 even carried a hopeful headline: organic net sales up 2.4%, sales "returned to growth." Peel the label and the picture darkens. Total net sales actually fell 1.9% to $2,787.8 million, the gap being divestitures shrinking the whole. Adjusted EPS dropped 23.5% to $0.39, adjusted operating margin fell more than 200 basis points, adjusted EBITDA shrank nearly 15%, and the company cut full-year guidance to the bottom of its range. The 2.4% was price/mix (+1.9pts) over volume (+0.5pts) — a pricing lever near the end of its travel. Through all of it management held a $1.40 dividend against falling profit and $7.3 billion of net debt; the nine-percent-plus yield is the market pricing the question of whether it survives. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Hershey's 93% profit jump is a price hike wearing a compounder's costume](2026-06-18T1130-hershey.md) · _2026-06-18_

Hershey doubled GAAP net income to $435 million in Q1 2026 and lifted gross margin to 39.4% from 33.7% — a headline that reads like a turnaround. But that GAAP margin expansion is distorted by mark-to-market accounting on cocoa hedges; on the basis management itself prefers, adjusted gross margin actually fell 80 basis points to 40.4%. The entire move is roughly ten points of price realization on a roughly two-point volume decline — Hershey is shrinking the number of candy bars it sells to grow the dollars. Two of three segments saw operating income drop: salty snacks down 18%, International down 47% (the latter masked by a thin-margin acquisition). This is a cocoa-levered commodity price-taker pushing list prices through demand destruction to clear a 30%–35% adjusted-EPS bar, valued by the market as a serene secular compounder rather than the cyclical its own income statement reveals. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Texas Roadhouse trades at 27x earnings while beef inflation quietly eats its margin](2026-06-18T1100-texas-roadhouse.md) · _2026-06-18_

Texas Roadhouse is the rare casual-diner that still packs its lobbies — comparable sales up 7.1% with 4.5% more bodies through the door in Q1 2026, a feat almost no full-service chain can match. But strip away the traffic story and a colder arithmetic emerges: restaurant margin slipped to 16.3% of sales from 16.6% a year earlier, food costs jumped 122 basis points, and commodity inflation ran 6.2% with beef — the literal centerpiece of the menu — doing most of the damage. Management guides commodity inflation to 6%–7% for the year and 7%–8% in the current quarter. This is a company whose pricing power is real but deliberately restrained behind a value promise, and whose single largest input is the one commodity it cannot hedge away. At roughly 27 times trailing earnings, the market pays a growth-stock multiple for a business that is, on the margin line, a price-taker in the cattle market. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [CAVA trades at 175x earnings while its own guidance halves same-store growth](2026-06-18T1030-cava.md) · _2026-06-18_

CAVA is, by any honest measure, an excellent operator — and this piece concedes it plainly. Q1 fiscal 2026 brought revenue up 32.2% to $434.4 million, same-restaurant sales up 9.7%, traffic up 6.8%, Chipotle-grade 25.1% restaurant-level margins, 459 units at $3.0 million AUVs, a pristine balance sheet with ~$403 million cash and zero debt. There is no fraud here and nothing hidden. The problem is entirely the price: at roughly 175 times trailing earnings, the stock has already discounted a decade of flawless execution. Read the outlook and the company's own forecast undercuts two assumptions — full-year same-restaurant sales guided to a mid-single-digit range (roughly 4.5%–7%), about half the pace just printed, and restaurant-level margin guided down to 23.7%–24.3%. GAAP net income actually fell to $23.6 million from $25.7 million. The question is not whether CAVA is good; it is whether anything less than perfect is already priced for catastrophe. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Tractor Supply's growth is rented from new stores while its old ones lose customers](2026-06-18T1000-tractor-supply.md) · _2026-06-18_

Tractor Supply sells a story of secular rural strength — 2,300-plus stores, a 40-million-member Neighbor's Club, decades of compounding. Strip away new-store openings and Q1 fiscal 2026 reveals a chain whose existing boxes are quietly leaking shoppers. Net sales rose 3.6% to $3.59 billion, yet comparable-store sales crept up only 0.5%, and that thin gain was entirely a pricing artifact: average ticket up 1.6% against transactions down 1.0%. Fewer people walked in; the ones who did paid more. Earnings actually fell — diluted EPS of $0.31 versus $0.34, net income down to $164.5 million from $179.4 million — even as the top line grew, on SG&A deleverage. The market dropped the stock roughly 10% on the print. This is the bought-growth-masks-organic-stall tell: when same-store traffic is negative and profit shrinks while sales rise, the "growth" is largely the cost of opening doors faster than the old doors can fill. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Floor & Decor sells more stores than flooring as comps fall 3.7% on a frozen housing market](2026-06-18T0930-floor-decor.md) · _2026-06-18_

Floor & Decor opened six warehouses in a quarter when its existing ones sold less, and that single sentence is the whole forensic problem. First-quarter fiscal 2026 net sales of $1.15 billion fell 0.7% even as the store base swelled to 276 boxes; comparable-store sales dropped 3.7%, transactions fell 5.5%, diluted EPS slid 17.8% to $0.37 from $0.45 — and management still reaffirmed twenty new openings for the year. The only thing holding the top line up is building stores faster than existing ones shrink: a denominator story dressed as a growth story. The stock trades near 22 times forward and roughly 24 times trailing earnings against a specialty-retail group near 11 times, a premium underwritten entirely by a housing-turnover recovery that has not arrived — existing-home sales sat at a 30-year low of 4.06 million in 2025, frozen by rate lock-in. This is a cyclical hard-surface flooring retailer priced as a secular grower. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Dollar Tree's 38% EPS jump rests on a tariff windfall and a price moat it already abandoned](2026-06-18T0900-dollar-tree.md) · _2026-06-18_

Dollar Tree closed its Family Dollar mistake on July 5, 2025, and the market re-rated the survivor as a clean compounder: 7.2% sales growth, comps of 3.5%, gross margin up 120 basis points, and adjusted EPS up 38% to $1.74 in the quarter ended May 2, 2026. Read the 10-Q and a different story appears. The traffic line is negative, minus 1.0%; the growth is ticket, plus 4.5% — the company is charging more. The famous fixed-price moat, everything for a buck, is gone, replaced by a $1.25-to-$7 ladder now marketed as a feature, which drops Dollar Tree into the DG/FIVE/WMT value brawl. And the headline beat leans on a roughly $110 million tariff refund plus freight and shrink tailwinds that reverse as easily as they arrived. At a forward multiple near 17 on $6.90 of hoped-for earnings, the stock is priced as if the cleanup is the whole story. It is the setup. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Dollar General's margin recovery runs on shrink math, not a richer customer](2026-06-18T0830-dollar-general.md) · _2026-06-18_

Wall Street cheered Dollar General's June quarter: net sales up 3.4% to $10.79 billion, gross margin a fat 31.6%, operating profit up 10.8% to $638.5 million, and a raised full-year outlook to $7.20–$7.45. The recovery narrative is intact and the stock has roughly doubled off its 2024 lows. But pull the margin apart and a quieter story appears. Same-store sales grew just 2.0%, traffic 1.4%, ticket a thin 0.5% — barely ahead of inflation. The profit that thrilled the Street came overwhelmingly from inside the warehouse, not the cash register: lower shrink, lower damages, better markups. That is a real but finite well. The forensic question is whether a company earning 5.9% operating margins off a financially stretched core customer has found a durable engine — or simply harvested the easy half of a self-help story while the customer underneath stays broke. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Deckers' Hoka cools to 15% as a two-brand empire prices in perfection](2026-06-17T1300-deckers.md) · _2026-06-17_

Deckers closed a record $5.47 billion fiscal 2026 (+10%) with a 23%-plus operating margin, but the forensic story is deceleration, not strength. Hoka — the engine that once compounded north of 27% a year — grew 16% for the full year to $2.59 billion and 15% in its largest-ever quarter ($671 million), then guided to "low double digits" and a single high-single-digit June quarter on "wholesale timing shifts." Ugg, the other half of a company where two brands are roughly 97% of revenue, is a seasonal boot brand guided to mid-single digits. Management's new through-2030 framework quietly resets the whole story to a high-single-digit revenue CAGR, with forward gross margin guided down to ~56.5% against $120 million of tariffs, rising freight, and a competitive squeeze from On above and Nike below. At roughly 15x forward earnings after a hard de-rating, the stock is no longer priced for perfection — but the smooth glide path still is. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Williams-Sonoma trades at 25 times earnings on a housing market that won't move](2026-06-17T1230-williams-sonoma.md) · _2026-06-17_

Williams-Sonoma posted a genuinely strong first quarter — comparable brand revenue up 4.8%, a 44.0% gross margin, $1.93 diluted EPS, $373 million returned to shareholders — off a best-in-class operating model that earns a 16-to-18% margin selling sofas and dinnerware. But the stock changes hands near $227, roughly 25 times trailing earnings, a software-like multiple on the most housing-levered, big-ticket, discretionary cash flow in retail. Existing-home sales sit frozen near 4.1 million against a 5-million norm, and the 4.8% comp is a share-gain number inside a market growing maybe 2% — West Elm's 8.5% masks Pottery Barn's 1.0%. Gross margin already fell 30 bps and operating margin 60 bps year over year against tariffs the company says peak in Q2. This is cyclical, housing-cycle earnings priced as a secular software annuity; the margins are real, but the multiple is paying for a thaw that has not arrived. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Lululemon Grows Revenue 4% While Profit Collapses 37% and the Americas Bleed](2026-06-17T1200-lululemon.md) · _2026-06-17_

Lululemon's first quarter of fiscal 2026 grew net revenue 4% to $2.47 billion — but income from operations fell 37% to $276.9 million, net income dropped to $195 million from $314.6 million, and operating margin compressed 730 basis points to 11.2%. The 4% headline is a denominator trick: comparable sales were negative on a constant-dollar basis, the Americas posted their fifth straight quarter of comp declines, and China (revenue +30% to $478.4 million) is carrying essentially all consolidated growth. Gross margin fell 410 bps to 54.2%, and the appearance of markdowns in that bridge is the first hard evidence the pricing moat is leaking against Alo and Vuori. Management cut full-year guidance for the second time, now projecting flat-to-down revenue and roughly $11 EPS against the $14 it once promised. A secular compounder is turning out to be a saturating one, and a 40%-plus YTD decline may not be the last cut. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Guardant Health races to $1.3B in revenue while losses keep widening past $110M a quarter](2026-06-17T1130-guardant.md) · _2026-06-17_

Guardant Health booked the fastest revenue growth of its public life — 48% to $302 million in Q1 2026, with Shield screening revenue up more than 600% to $41.6 million — yet its GAAP net loss widened to $112.1 million from $95.2 million a year earlier. The company burned $233 million of free cash flow in 2025 and funds its screening land grab with stock-based comp and capital raises (over $700 million of fresh equity and convertible debt in late 2025) rather than profits. The bull case is TAM math: tens of millions of unscreened Americans at a $1,495 Medicare rate. The forensic case is the gap between that TAM and the P&L — plus a clinical asterisk (Shield's advanced-adenoma sensitivity of just 13.2% versus Cologuard Plus in the low-40s) and deeper-pocketed rivals in Exact Sciences and a circling Abbott. This is a story about the distance between a market a company is priced for and the income statement it actually reports. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Tempus AI grows revenue 36% to $348M yet GAAP losses widen to $126M](2026-06-17T1100-tempus.md) · _2026-06-17_

Tempus AI sells an "intelligent diagnostics" genomics-flywheel story, and the Q1 2026 top line is genuinely fast: revenue of $348.1 million, up roughly 36%, full-year guidance lifted to $1.59–$1.60 billion. But underneath sits a GAAP net loss of $125.9 million in a single quarter — nearly double the $68.0 million a year earlier — while the company paid $56.3 million in stock-based comp and absorbed $32.3 million of unrealized securities losses. Losses are compounding faster than sales, and the 36% growth partly reflects the acquired Ambry Genetics revenue base, not pure organic momentum. Short-seller Spruce Point has alleged the AI label overstates a business mostly built on reimbursed diagnostics and flagged related-party concerns around a Pathos AI data deal — these are clearly labeled allegations Tempus disputes, not adjudicated findings. The stock around $55–$56 is priced as a secular AI compounder with no public date for GAAP profit. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Instacart's first $1B quarter ran on ads, not delivery — and the engine is cooling](2026-06-17T1030-instacart.md) · _2026-06-17_

Instacart (Maplebear, CART) crossed $1 billion in quarterly revenue for the first time in Q1 2026 — gross transaction value of $10.29 billion (+13%), GAAP net income of $144 million (+36%), $300 million of adjusted EBITDA, a $3.5 billion buyback. Look past the milestone and a colder structure appears. The delivery business clears a flat ~7.1% transaction take rate on the goods it moves — thin and contested against DoorDash, Uber, and Amazon. The profit Wall Street cheers comes overwhelmingly from a $286 million advertising machine selling shelf placement back to the brands whose products it delivers, and that engine, though it grew 16% (its fastest since 2023), is guided to slow to 11–14% next quarter as GTV growth decelerates to 11–13%. The stock fell roughly 8% on the print. This is what happens when the ad flywheel that masks thin delivery economics starts, quietly, to spin slower. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Upstart's revenue jumped 44% in Q1 while its GAAP loss widened and its AI model faces a fraud suit](2026-06-17T1000-upstart.md) · _2026-06-17_

Upstart sells the idea that its AI underwrites credit better than a FICO score and therefore deserves a software multiple immune to the credit cycle. Q1 2026 complicates that. Revenue climbed 44% to $308 million and originations leapt 61% to roughly $3.4 billion — genuinely impressive — yet the company posted a wider GAAP net loss of $6.6 million, its adjusted-EBITDA margin collapsed from 20% to 13%, and roughly a billion dollars of loans sat on its own balance sheet. The surging growth reads as a cyclical macro-window recovery dressed as a smarter model, with stock-based comp bridging the GAAP loss to a non-GAAP "profit." Above it all hangs a securities class action alleging executives overstated the accuracy of the very "Model 22" engine that is the entire equity story — clearly labeled as allegations, not adjudicated findings. At a price-to-sales multiple this rich, there is almost no room for the credit cycle to do what it always eventually does. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Roku finally turned a GAAP profit — but stock comp still dwarfs it, and the boxes still sell at a loss](2026-06-17T0930-roku.md) · _2026-06-17_

After five years of losses, Roku crossed into black ink: $88.4 million of GAAP net income on $4.74 billion of 2025 revenue, then $85.7 million more in Q1 2026 on revenue up 22% to $1.25 billion, with 100 million streaming households and an ad business compounding near 28%. The lazy "Roku doesn't make money" short is now dead — so the forensic frame pivots to the architecture of the win. Stock-based compensation ran $354 million in 2025, roughly four times the entire reported profit. The devices that recruit those households carry a negative 16.3% gross margin, a loss-leader subsidy that has only deepened. And the high-margin ad dollars financing the whole edifice now sit directly in the crosshairs of Amazon, Google, and Netflix, all selling connected-TV inventory at scale. This is a real business that has reached a thin, contested, dilution-financed profit — and is priced as if the contest is already over. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Pinterest Grew Revenue 18% and Still Slid Into a GAAP Loss as 367 Million Users Pay 20 Cents](2026-06-17T0900-pinterest.md) · _2026-06-17_

Pinterest's Q1 2026 looked like the moment the commerce engine finally caught: revenue of $1.008 billion up 18%, monthly active users at a record 631 million, $207 million of adjusted EBITDA, raised Q2 guidance. But the 18% gain arrived as a $73.6 million GAAP net loss, because the adjusted number only exists after stripping out ~$231 million of stock-based comp (about 23% of revenue) plus ~$47 million of restructuring. Almost all the user growth is a Rest-of-World cohort monetizing at twenty cents a head against $7.12 in North America — record reach where the money is thinnest. And Pinterest is leaning on Amazon (its first-ever third-party ad partner) and Google — its two largest competitors — to backfill demand its own sales force cannot. A $3.5 billion buyback funded partly by Elliott's $1 billion mostly mops up self-created dilution. The bulls are buying an option on a shoppable-commerce future the financials have not yet built. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [Snap's ad engine grew 3% while Meta's grew 33%, and the gap is the whole story](2026-06-17T0830-snap.md) · _2026-06-17_

Snap closed Q1 2026 with a turnaround-shaped headline — revenue up 12% to $1.53 billion, daily users back to growth at 483 million, the net loss cut from $140 million to $89 million — and a footnote that reads like a confession. Strip out the 87%-growth "other revenue" line ($285 million of subscriptions and a now-terminated Perplexity AI deal) and the actual advertising business that is supposed to justify the valuation grew exactly 3% to roughly $1.24 billion. In the same quarter, Meta's family-of-apps advertising grew 33% — a tenfold gap in the one number that matters, the signature of a price-taker losing share in an auction a giant sets. Quarterly stock-based comp and related payroll of $263 million exceeds the $233 million of adjusted EBITDA it is excluded from, and Snap has produced no full year of GAAP profit in eight years public. The turnaround is real at the margin and illusory at the core, propped up by subscriptions and a $2,195 pair of AR glasses it is betting the company on. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.

### [MongoDB reaccelerates to 25% growth, but its $4.4M GAAP profit rests on a $493M stock subsidy](2026-06-16T1300-mongodb.md) · _2026-06-16_

MongoDB stunned the bears with a Q1 FY27 reacceleration to 25% growth — $687.6 million in revenue, the fastest first-quarter print in three years — and its first sliver of GAAP net income at $4.4 million. Strip back the reconciliation and a more delicate machine appears. Operations still lost $24.8 million on a GAAP basis; the $4.4 million of net income exists only because non-operating items rescued an operating loss. The $112.3 million the company calls "non-GAAP net income" is built by adding back the better part of a half-billion dollars (~$493.9M) in annual stock-based compensation. Atlas — three-quarters of the business — is consumption revenue that flexes with somebody else's application traffic. At roughly ten times sales and eighty-times forward non-GAAP earnings, MongoDB is priced as though the reacceleration is structural rather than a single, macro-flattered quarter. Fact-checked; see `audit/`.
